</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of postal codes in Germany</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:German_postcode_information.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/German_postcode_information.png/350px-German_postcode_information.png" width="350" height="472" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/German_postcode_information.png/525px-German_postcode_information.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/German_postcode_information.png/700px-German_postcode_information.png 2x" data-file-width="902" data-file-height="1216" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:German_postcode_information.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German Postleitzahl map of the first two digits. The green lines mark state borders which do not correspond with postal code areas.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Postal codes in Germany</b>, <i>Postleitzahl</i> (plural Postleitzahlen, abbreviated to PLZ; literally "postal routing number"), since 1 July 1993 consist of five digits. The first two digits indicate the wider area, the last three digits the postal district.</p>
<p>Before reunification, both the <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">Federal Republic of Germany</a> (FRG) and the <a href="/wiki/German_Democratic_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="German Democratic Republic">German Democratic Republic</a> (GDR) used four-digit <a href="/wiki/Postal_code" title="Postal code">codes</a>. Under a transitional arrangement following reunification, between 1989 and 1993 postal codes in the west were prefixed with 'W', e.g.: <b>W-1000 [Berlin] 30</b> (postal districts in western cities were separate from the postal code) and those in the east with 'O' (for <i>Ost</i>), e.g.: <b>O-1xxx Berlin</b>.</p>
<p>City administrations and postal customers with high mail volumes, or <i>Gro√ükunden</i> have their own postal codes, separate from those used for postal districts or PO Box number ranges.</p>
<p>Postal regions do not necessarily follow <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">state</a> boundaries, so sorting by state is not practical.</p>
<p>The postal regions and some postal codes are:</p>
<div style="clear: right; margin-bottom: .5em; float: right; padding: .5em 0 .8em 1.4em; background: none; width: auto;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="25000-25999">25000-25999</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_postal_codes_in_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: 25000-25999">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The region 25 covers all of <a href="/wiki/Schleswig-Holstein" title="Schleswig-Holstein">Schleswig-Holstein</a>'s westcoast from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Danish</a> border. All mail from, to and within this region is handled by the postal distribution center in <a href="/wiki/Elmshorn" title="Elmshorn">Elmshorn</a>.</p>
